      <div class="article collapsable-panel" data-story_id="1349386" id="article-1">
       <div class="meta share-expanded">

        <p class="date">
         Thu Dec 04, 2014 at 10:31 AM PST
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2014/12/04/1349386/-New-lie-in-the-shooting-death-of-Tamir-Rice-discovered-Police-never-saw-the-tip-of-the-gun-at-all" id="titleHref">
          New lie in the shooting death of Tamir Rice discovered: Police never saw the tip of the gun at all
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/Shaun King">
          Shaun King
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=1128171&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
         <span class="for">
          for
         </span>
         <a href="/blog/Shaun King">
          shaunking
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/12/04/1349386/-New-lie-in-the-shooting-death-of-Tamir-Rice-discovered-Police-never-saw-the-tip-of-the-gun-at-all" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="New lie in the shooting death of Tamir Rice discovered: Police never saw the tip of the gun at all" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/12/04/1349386/-New-lie-in-the-shooting-death-of-Tamir-Rice-discovered-Police-never-saw-the-tip-of-the-gun-at-all" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="223" data-story_id="1349386" href="/story/2014/12/04/1349386/-New-lie-in-the-shooting-death-of-Tamir-Rice-discovered-Police-never-saw-the-tip-of-the-gun-at-all#comments">
           223 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <div class="dkimg-c">
          <span class="image_container">
           <img alt="" height="366" src="http://images.dailykos.com/images/118622/large/cleveland-police-shoot-boy.jpg?1417716699" width="550"/>
          </span>
         </div>
         When Officer Timothy Loehmann shot and killed 12-year-old Tamir Rice on November 22, an immediate coverup of his misconduct began.
         <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/12/02/1348833/-Tamir-Rice-The-story-behind-the-execution-character-assassination-coverup-of-a-senseless-murder">
          At least five lies
         </a>
         have already been uncovered, but the latest suggests the entire Cleveland Police Department is in on it.
         <p>
          The Sunday after Tamir Rice was killed, Cleveland Police
          <a href="http://www.cleveland.com/metro/index.ssf/2014/11/12-year-old_boy_shot_by_clevel_1.html">
           held a press conference
          </a>
          in which they displayed the toy air pistol they say was possessed by Tamir Rice.
          <a href="http://www.toledoblade.com/State/2014/11/24/Cleveland-boy-with-fake-pistol-killed-by-police.html">
           In this press conference,
          </a>
          Detective Jennifer Ciaccia, who also serves as a spokesperson for the department, emphasized that the "orange tip" of the gun was missing and that the "the police learned the gun was fake after the shooting."
         </p>
         <p>
          The thing, is, though, the police never even saw Tamir Rice brandish or point the pistol at them to determine if the orange cap was actually missing or not. When Detective Ciaccia made the repeated statements that the orange cap was missing, she did so in an effort to bolster the claim that the police had no choice but to fire because they saw the weapon, couldn't determine with their eyes that it was a fake, and acted on instincts to protect themselves. This simply is not true.
         </p>
         <p>
          As you will see from the video below the fold, when the police pulled up on Tamir Rice, they shoot him in less than two seconds. In that encounter, the gun is never drawn for them to see the missing cap one way or the other.
         </p>
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">
         <p>
          <iframe defang_border="no" height="500" scrolling="no" src="http://player.theplatform.com/p/7wvmTC/MSNBCEmbeddedOffSite?guid=n_hayes_Btam_141201_402600" width="635">
          </iframe>
          <br/>
         </p>
         <p>
          <br/>
          Now, we learn that Officer Timothy Loehmann was actually declared unfit for duty before he transferred to the Cleveland Police Department.
          <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2014/dec/03/officer-who-fatally-shot-tamir-rice-had-been-judged-unfit?CMP=share_btn_tw">
           In an excellent report
          </a>
          from Tom McCarthy from
          <i>
           The Guardian
          </i>
          , we learn damning details about Officer Loehmann:
          <br/>
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          During a state range qualification course, Ptl Loehmann was distracted and weepy, Polak wrote, naming the trainer as Sgt Tinnirello. [Loehmann] could not follow simple directions, could not communicate clear thoughts nor recollections, and his handgun performance was dismal. Sgt Tinnirello tried to work through this with Ptl Loehmann by giving him some time. But, after some talking it was clear to Sgt Tinnirello that the recruit was just not mentally prepared to be doing firearm training.
          <p>
           In recommending Loehmanns dismissal, Polak listed what he said were other performance shortcomings, including Loehmanns having left his gun unlocked, lied to supervisors and failed to follow orders.
          </p>
          <p>
           Due to this dangerous loss of composure during live range training and his inability to manage this personal stress, I do not believe Ptl Loehmann shows the maturity needed to work in our employment, Polak concludes. For these reasons, I am recommending he be released from the employment of the city of Independence.
           <strong>
            I do not believe time, nor training, will be able to change or correct these deficiencies
           </strong>
           .
          </p>
         </blockquote>
        </div>
       </div>
       <h4>

	#popup-story_setTags div.content-bar a:visited	{ color: #7C470C }
        </style>
        <br/>
        <div>
         <p>
          Add keywords that describe this diary.
		Separate multiple keywords with commas.
          <br/>
          <a href="/special/tag_tips" target="_blank">
           Tagging tips
          </a>
          -
          <a href="/search?search_tags=1" target="_blank">
           Search For Tags
          </a>
          -
          <a href="http://www.dkosopedia.com/wiki/Tag:Tagfinder" target="_blank">
           Browse For Tags
          </a>
         </p>
         <div class="pageTip hasTooltip" style="margin-top:3px">
          ?
         </div>
         <div class="tooltipContents qtip-style-dk4_large qtip-pos-br">
          <p>
           <b>
            More Tagging tips:
           </b>
          </p>
          <p>
           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>
         </div>
         <!-- &lt;h4 id="p_tagErrorMessage"&gt;You must enter at least one Tag for this Diary Entry:&lt;/h4&gt; -->
         <p>
          <input id="p_tagInput" name="tag_draft" size="70" type="text" value=""/>
          <!-- &lt;input id="tagSubmit" type="submit" name="submit" value="Submit" /&gt; -->
         </p>
         <p style="font-style:italic">
          Consider if one or more of these tags fits your diary:
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Civil Rights');return false;">
           Civil Rights
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Community');return false;">
           Community
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Congress');return false;">
           Congress
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Culture');return false;">
           Culture
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Economy');return false;">
           Economy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Education');return false;">
           Education
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Elections');return false;">
           Elections
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Energy');return false;">
           Energy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Environment');return false;">
           Environment
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Health Care');return false;">
           Health Care
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('International');return false;">
           International
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Labor');return false;">
           Labor
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Law');return false;">
           Law
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Media');return false;">
           Media
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Meta');return false;">
           Meta
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('National Security');return false;">
           National Security
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Science');return false;">
           Science
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Transportation');return false;">
           Transportation
          </a>
          , or
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('White House');return false;">
           White House
          </a>
          .
	If your diary is specific to a state, consider adding the state 
	(
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('California');return false;">
           California
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Texas');return false;">
           Texas
          </a>
          , etc).
	Keep in mind, though, that there are many wonderful and important diaries
	that don't fit in any of these tags. Don't worry if yours doesn't.
         </p>

            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">

              <a href="/user/uid:982198">

              </a>

              <a href="/user/uid:1104434">
               dhdschll
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:1082509">
               Maggiemad
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             14 year old kid, playing at a school yard with friends. police respond to a call that said that some boys are at the school and are playing with a gun. cops arrive, kids run, one cop chases 14 year old to a fenced in part of the school. what happens next nobody knows for sure. the cop claimed the kid turned on him and was grabbing for a gun, so he shot and killed him. autopsy showed the kid was hit in the back and the side.
            </p>
            <p>
             the copy was tried and acquitted of course. at trial a big deal was made of the bullet holes in the jacket and if they really showed that the kid had his back to the cop or if they showed he was turning as if to fire a gun.
            </p>
            <p>
             that case is 24 years old, from a generic New Jersey suburb. and the story hasn't changed. situations that can and are de-escalated all the time end up being mainlined to deadly force when a black youth is involved, and the people responsible will never admit why or hold anyone accountable.
            </p>

          <li id="c140">
           <div class="cx" id="cx55148778">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              My first encounter with a cop was when
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1349386/55148778#c140?mode=alone;showrate=1#c140">
               2+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:165753">
                TKO333
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:1146709">
                HarpPlayer
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              I was 18. I was riding my brand new fully legal motorcycle down the road when a friend on his pulled up beside meat a stop sign. We both turned left going about 100 yards before my friend turned off. I continued another 100 yards to the stop sign where suddenly there was a sheriff car with lights on, no siren so big in the mirrors I thought for sure I was going to get hit and killed. I turned out directly around the stop sign to both get out of his way and allow him to proceed since it was still not clear he was after me. As I sat there for a split second Deputy Dogg jumped out of the vehicle in the middle of the street with gun drawn over the top of his car shouting don't move turn off your engine. I was bewildered and shocked that I could be gunned down for riding my bike fully legal and insured without any reason whatsoever for such an assault. After showing all my ID, etc I was released without so much as a warning. This is imprinted on my mind so deeply that every time I see a cop doing his duty I watch for the same signs I experienced in my first encounter. Sadly I see the exact same tendency for them to act like steroid shooting bullies nearly every time. I myself have employed the "chokehold" 3 times in my life, once when assaulted in a bar by some dimwit that thought I was flirting with his woman when I was actually dancing with another girl at the time. I got broken glasses and a black eye from his sucker punch, he damned near got strangled. I could have broken his neck or choked him unconscious but instead just controlled him till police got there. Both the 2nd and 3rd were breaking up fights for the good of all concerned.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="cf">
             <p class="sig">
             </p>
             <p class="cb">
              by
              <a href="/user/uid:1097114">
               kevinkosnerd
              </a>
              on
              <a href="/comments/1349386/55148778#c140">
               Fri Dec 05, 2014 at 01:48:05 PM PST
              </a>
             </p>

             </p>

              Left an unsecured weapon overnight in the police station in contravention of protocols.
             </p>

             </p>
             <p>

             </p>
             <p>
              His Deputy Chief said that while he smart enough to understand why these issues are problems, he was too emotionally immature recognize the seriousness of the situation and recommended that he be let go.
             </p>
             <p>
              This is case of a kid who came from a family of police officers, but wasn't cutout to be one. I just wonder how many favors were called in to get him through the academy.

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               The guy just didn't fit the job, apparently, at least not at this time in his life. Sometimes the kind thing is actually to give someone the harsh truth and stop cutting them slack. It sounds like the best thing the department could have done was tell him "look, I know you're from a family of cops, but not everyone's got the temperament for it, and there's no shame in that. Go spend some time finding yourself and getting your head sorted out."
              </p>
              <p>
               If they'd done that, maybe two lives could have been saved.
              </p>
              <p>
               Had a college prof tell me something similar once, probably some of the best advice I've gotten in my life.
              </p>

              <div class="ct">
               <p>
                compassion for someone who wants something because he thinks he should even when unfit. I know how getting dumped can mess with your emotions.
               </p>
               <p>
                But I don't carry a gun on the job and deal with sorting actual danger from a kid with an air gun, and when you've had as much evidence as this young man had shoved in his face that he was unfit, his wants just fade into unimportance. His situation is like a two year persisting in a tantrum, add a loaded gun and a 12 year old is dead and will never get to grow up, get to choose a career, etc. When you weigh the two, the cop isn't the sad story here. Its an abdication of personal responsibility and public responsibility by the department that hired him without checking why he was flushed from his hometown pd, and not recognizing the symptoms sooner.
               </p>

          <li id="c115">
           <div class="cx" id="cx55144675">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              I'm getting so tired of online apologists
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1349386/55144675#c115?mode=alone;showrate=1#c115">
               3+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:1162163">
                Liberalleycat
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:982198">
                Againststochasticterrorism
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:1082509">
                Maggiemad
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              ... for police abuse carrying out metaphorical lynchings of the victims.
             </p>
             <p>
              The police had no reason and no right to do what they did. Very simple. They are SUPPOSED to be trained in (a) de-escalation tactics (which they seem to have no problem using if the person in question is white) and in (b) escalation of force rules.
             </p>
             <p>
              They are NEVER supposed to go straight from seeing a person to killing them - not even if that person is big and agitated (clearly not the case in this instance), or reaching for their waistband, or walking with their hands in their pockets, or holding a gun.
             </p>
             <p>
              There is no part of their training, or of the law, or of morality that makes it acceptable.
             </p>
             <p>
              Lack of compliance is not a death penalty offense.
             </p>
             <p>
              Playing with a toy in the park is not a death penalty offense.
             </p>
             <p>
              Talking back to an officer (even with bad language) is not a death penalty offense.
             </p>
             <p>
              And EVEN IF someone ACTUALLY commits a death penalty offense, they're STILL not supposed to be killed
              <strong>
               by the police
              </strong>
              - that penalty is supposed to be carried out
              <em>
               after a trial
              </em>
              proves guilt.
             </p>
             <p>
              We do not have laws that say extra-judicial execution is acceptable. Though we do, apparently, have a reality in which the DA and grand juries collude to make it de-facto acceptable.
             </p>
            </div>

           <p class="cb">
            by

             Oil the Poil

        <li id="c164">
         <div class="cx" id="cx55155540">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Be a responsible parent
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1349386/55155540#c164?mode=alone;showrate=1#c164">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Not that I condone the actions of the police some of the time (and I have seen some actions that I totally disagreed with), having worked in law enforcement I have seen the other side of the coin.....when you are called to a scene that is involving a person with a gun you go into automatic defensive training. Now even though the person was a kid, it was reported by the dispatcher that he had a gun (and it has been reported looked like a real gun).....the dispatcher
            <strong>
             DID NOT
            </strong>
            report to the officer
            <strong>
             EVERYTHING
            </strong>
            that the caller had stated "may be a child and not sure if it is a real gun or not" which could have possibly resulted in a different outcome to the Cleveland child shooting.
           </p>
           <p>
            Parents need to teach their children that even though it is a toy gun....
            <strong>
             DO NOT point it at other people in a threatening manner
            </strong>
            . If a parent is going to get their child a toy that looks like a real gun then they need to make sure the child is responsible enough to have it and understand the potential outcome of being stupid with it. In my opinion race and sex of the person does not matter when an officer pulls up on a scene that has been reported as "a person with a gun" and they see someone with a gun that refuses to follow the officers orders to drop the weapon. In most cases the adrenalin rush takes over and you have only a split second to make a decision on whether you are going to become a target of the weapon.
           </p>
           <p>
            From the news reports I have read and videos released, I do question why the officer responded the way he did but also would have to ask the dispatcher why he/she did not report what was stated by the caller that it may be a child and may be a toy gun. Having had 911 training I understand the importance of relaying ALL the information you are given and how not reporting it all to the officer could have a dramatic impact on the outcome of a situation. Unfortunately the outcome was a tragic loss of a child's life and the officer is going to have to live with the consequences of his actions for the rest of his life.
           </p>
           <p>
            I do believe there are officers out here that take the power of being"
            <strong>
             the police
            </strong>
            " to far and should not be wearing a badge and carrying a gun but there are a lot more GOOD officers than bad ones. Where would this country be without the law?
            <br/>
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">

        <li id="c219">
         <div class="cx" id="cx55163330">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Police Procedure
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1349386/55163330#c219?mode=alone;showrate=1#c219">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            You respond to a man with a gun call. You DON"T pull up exposing yourself or your partner to the person with the supposed gun. The so called training officer pulls up exposing the rookie to the person and it is no wonder the rookie panics. Use the squad car as cover. Nose in, stay back, exit the car and use the doors for cover as you tell the person to raise his hands. What is happening to police training.
           </p>

  function loadChartbeat() {
    window._sf_endpt=(new Date()).getTime();
    var e = document.createElement('script');
    e.setAttribute('language', 'javascript');
    e.setAttribute('type', 'text/javascript');
    e.setAttribute('src',
       (("https:" == document.location.protocol) ? "https://a248.e.akamai.net/chartbeat.download.akamai.com/102508/" : "http://static.chartbeat.com/") +
       "js/chartbeat.js");
    document.body.appendChild(e);
  }
  var oldonload = window.onload;
  window.onload = (typeof window.onload != 'function') ?
     loadChartbeat : function() { oldonload(); loadChartbeat(); };

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
  </script>
